## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, potentially with various orders and complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration, e.g., surface-catalyzed reactions at saturation'}
- {'name': 'First-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition'}
- {'name': 'Second-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Bimolecular reaction where two molecules of same species react'}
- {'name': 'nth-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'General power-law rate expression for fractional or arbitrary reaction order'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'Forward and reverse first-order reactions approaching equilibrium'}
- {'name': 'Reversible second-order/first-order', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2', 'scenario': 'Quadratic rate law from reversible or competing reactions'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Product-catalyzed reaction where B = c1 - A acts as catalyst'}
- {'name': 'Substrate inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme kinetics with substrate inhibition at high concentrations'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics (Langmuir-Hinshelwood)', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2', 'scenario': 'Surface reaction kinetics with competitive adsorption'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent deactivation rate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Reaction with catalyst deactivation or time-varying rate constant'}
- {'name': 'Parallel reaction kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Simultaneous first and second order consumption pathways'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2', 'scenario': 'nth-order kinetics with a constant source or sink term'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction intermediate', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t)', 'scenario': 'Rate of change for intermediate species in sequential A→B→C reactions'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate (consumption) with power-law dependence on concentration → dA_dt = -k * A^n indicating nth-order irreversible reaction
- Linear dependence of rate on concentration → first-order kinetics, check for exponential decay in A(t)
- Rate approaching zero as concentration approaches a nonzero equilibrium value → reversible reaction with equilibrium constant, look for (A - A_eq) terms
- Rate expression with both positive and negative terms in different powers of A → competing or reversible reactions with different orders
- Rate that depends on both A and (constant - A) → conservation law constraint, closed system with autocatalysis or reversible stoichiometry
- Concentration-independent rate at high A but linear at low A → saturation kinetics, rational function A/(A + K)
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → equilibrium point, look for polynomial roots in A
- Explicit time dependence in rate beyond what A(t) provides → non-autonomous system, catalyst deactivation, or external forcing
